<p><b>Hull Paragon Interchange</b> is an integrated rail, bus and coach station in the city centre of <a href="/wiki/Kingston_upon_Hull" title="Kingston upon Hull">Kingston upon Hull</a>, England. The <a href="/wiki/G.T._Andrews" class="mw-redirect" title="G.T. Andrews">G.T. Andrews</a>-designed station was originally named <i>Paragon Station</i>, and together with the adjoining Station Hotel, it opened in 1847 as the new Hull terminus for the growing traffic of the <a href="/wiki/York_and_North_Midland_Railway" title="York and North Midland Railway">York and North Midland</a> (Y&amp;NMR) leased to the <a href="/wiki/Hull_and_Selby_Railway" title="Hull and Selby Railway">Hull and Selby Railway</a> (H&amp;S).<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> As well as trains to the west, the station was the terminus of the Y&amp;NMR and H&amp;S railway's <a href="/wiki/Hull_to_Scarborough_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Hull to Scarborough Line">Hull to Scarborough Line</a>. From the 1860s the station also became the terminus of the <a href="/wiki/Hull_and_Holderness_Railway" title="Hull and Holderness Railway">Hull and Holderness</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hull_and_Hornsea_Railway" title="Hull and Hornsea Railway">Hull and Hornsea</a> railways.
</p><p>At the beginning of the 20th&#160;century the <a href="/wiki/North_Eastern_Railway_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="North Eastern Railway (UK)">North Eastern Railway</a> (NER) expanded the trainshed and station to the designs of <a href="/wiki/William_Bell_(architect)" title="William Bell (architect)">William Bell</a>, installing the present five arched span platform roof. In 1962 a modernist office block Paragon House was installed above the station main entrance, replacing a 1900s iron canopy; the offices were initially used as regional headquarters for <a href="/wiki/British_Rail" title="British Rail">British Rail</a>.
</p><p>A bus station was erected adjacent to the north of the station in the mid 1930s. In the early 2000s plans for an integrated bus and rail station were made, as part of a larger development including a shopping centre; <a href="/wiki/St_Stephen%27s_Hull" title="St Stephen&#39;s Hull">St Stephen's shopping centre</a>, a hotel, housing, and music and theatre facilities. The new station, named "Paragon Interchange" opened in September 2007, integrating the city's railway and bus stations under William Bell's 1900s trainshed.
</p><p>The station is currently operated by <a href="/wiki/TransPennine_Express" title="TransPennine Express">TransPennine Express</a>, which provides train services along with <a href="/wiki/Northern_(train_operating_company)" title="Northern (train operating company)">Northern</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hull_Trains" title="Hull Trains">Hull Trains</a> and <a href="/wiki/London_North_Eastern_Railway" title="London North Eastern Railway">London North Eastern Railway</a>.
</p>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-11"><a href="#Services"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Services</span></a>

</ul>
</li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Paragon_railway_station">Paragon railway station</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hull_Paragon_Interchange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Paragon railway station">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hull_Paragon_Interchange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1840 the <a href="/wiki/Hull_and_Selby_Railway" title="Hull and Selby Railway">Hull and Selby Railway</a> opened the first railway line into Hull, terminating at a passenger and goods terminal, <a href="/wiki/Manor_House_Street_railway_station" title="Manor House Street railway station">Manor House Street station</a>, adjacent to the <a href="/wiki/Humber_Dock" class="mw-redirect" title="Humber Dock">Humber Dock</a>, near the old town. Subsequently, the Hull and Selby Railway entered into working arrangements with the <a href="/wiki/Manchester_and_Leeds_Railway" title="Manchester and Leeds Railway">Manchester and Leeds Railway</a> and then the <a href="/wiki/York_and_North_Midland_Railway" title="York and North Midland Railway">York and North Midland Railway</a>. In 1845 an <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Parliament" title="Act of Parliament">Act of Parliament</a> enabled the York and North Midland and/or the Manchester and Leeds to take a lease of the company with an option to buy the line at a later date – only the York and North Midland was subsequently active. In 1846 the Hull and Selby completed its <a href="/wiki/Hull_and_Selby_Railway_(Bridlington_branch)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hull and Selby Railway (Bridlington branch)">Bridlington branch</a> which connected from a junction at <a href="/wiki/Dairycoates" title="Dairycoates">Dairycoates</a> near Hull to a line the York and North Midland was building from Bridlington to Seamer, connecting to its <a href="/wiki/York_to_Scarborough_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="York to Scarborough Line">York to Scarborough Line</a>, forming a railway route from Hull to <a href="/wiki/Scarborough,_North_Yorkshire" title="Scarborough, North Yorkshire">Scarborough</a> on the east coast.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="First_railway_station.2C_hotel_and_branches_.281848.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="First_railway_station,_hotel_and_branches_(1848)">First railway station, hotel and branches (1848)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hull_Paragon_Interchange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: First railway station, hotel and branches (1848)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hull_Paragon_Station_original_south_fascade.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Hull_Paragon_Station_original_south_fascade.jpg/220px-Hull_Paragon_Station_original_south_fascade.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Hull_Paragon_Station_original_south_fascade.jpg/330px-Hull_Paragon_Station_original_south_fascade.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Hull_Paragon_Station_original_south_fascade.jpg/440px-Hull_Paragon_Station_original_south_fascade.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2006" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hull_Paragon_Station_original_south_fascade.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The original southern entrance range (2014)</div></div></div>
<p>In 1846 the York and North Midland and Manchester and Leeds railways began proceedings to create a new terminal station and connecting branch line in Hull.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The "York and North Midland (Hull Station), 1847" act was subsequently passed.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;n 1&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The new station had the advantage of being better situated for travellers, and allowed the old station to be used exclusively for freight traffic. In addition the Hull and Selby company were keen to attract the investment in a new station from the leaseholders, as the capital investment was likely to increase the permanence of the relationship with the lessors.<sup id="cite_ref-turk_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-turk-6">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The branches to the station were constructed off the Bridlington branch: a branch turning north-east close to the line's crossing of the Hessle Road;<sup id="cite_ref-hrjn_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrjn-7">&#91;map 1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-os240_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-os240-8">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> and a branch turning south-east at 'Cottingham Junction' near to Haverflatts farm;<sup id="cite_ref-cj_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cj-9">&#91;map 2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> the two branches met at a junction 0.5 miles (0.8&#160;km) roughly west of the new station.<sup id="cite_ref-os240_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-os240-8">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> In addition a new connecting chord was made from the Hull and Selby Line,<sup id="cite_ref-hwj_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hwj-11">&#91;map 3&#93;</a></sup> to the Bridlington branch,<sup id="cite_ref-hrj_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrj-12">&#91;map 4&#93;</a></sup> allowing direct through running from the west into the new station.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The station was located on the western edge of the growing Georgian town, and took its name from "Paragon Street".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFawcett200186_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFawcett200186-14">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Construction contracts had been signed by early 1847, before the bill had been formally passed.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;n 2&#93;</a></sup> The station opened in 1847 without any notable ceremony.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESheahan1864572_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESheahan1864572-16">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The station and hotel were both in the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Renaissance_revival_architecture" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian Renaissance revival architecture">Italian Renaissance style</a>, with both <a href="/wiki/Doric_order" title="Doric order">Doric</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ionic_order" title="Ionic order">Ionic order</a> elements; the fascades show inspiration from the interior courtyard of the <a href="/wiki/Palazzo_Farnese" title="Palazzo Farnese">Palazzo Farnese</a>. The main station building was aligned east-west, south of the tracks, facing onto Anlaby Road – a two-storey centrally located booking hall was entered via a small <a href="/wiki/Porte-coch%C3%A8re" title="Porte-cochère">porte-cochère</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-se_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-se-17">&#91;map 5&#93;</a></sup> and flanked by 11 bay wide single storey wings, with two storey 3 bay buildings on either end, one a parcels office, the other the station master's house.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESheahan1864572_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESheahan1864572-16">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPevsnerNeave1995524_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPevsnerNeave1995524-18">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFawcett200186_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFawcett200186-14">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The train shed contained 5 tracks and 2 platforms, each 30 feet (9.1&#160;m), covered with a three span iron roof.<sup id="cite_ref-ps_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ps-19">&#91;map 6&#93;</a></sup> The station site was nearly 2.5 acres (1.0&#160;ha).<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;n 3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESheahan1864572_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESheahan1864572-16">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Paragon_station_(Royal_Station_Hotel)_early_1900s_or_before,_postcard.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Paragon_station_%28Royal_Station_Hotel%29_early_1900s_or_before%2C_postcard.jpg/220px-Paragon_station_%28Royal_Station_Hotel%29_early_1900s_or_before%2C_postcard.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Paragon_station_%28Royal_Station_Hotel%29_early_1900s_or_before%2C_postcard.jpg/330px-Paragon_station_%28Royal_Station_Hotel%29_early_1900s_or_before%2C_postcard.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Paragon_station_%28Royal_Station_Hotel%29_early_1900s_or_before%2C_postcard.jpg/440px-Paragon_station_%28Royal_Station_Hotel%29_early_1900s_or_before%2C_postcard.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1239" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Paragon_station_(Royal_Station_Hotel)_early_1900s_or_before,_postcard.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Station Hotel, with original <i><a href="/wiki/Porte-coch%C3%A8re" title="Porte-cochère">porte-cochère</a></i> entrance</div></div></div>
<p>The hotel was in a similar style to the station, located at the east end of the station with its main fascade and entrance facing east.<sup id="cite_ref-sh_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sh-21">&#91;map 7&#93;</a></sup> It was completed in 1849 as a three-storey building, 9 bays wide, of area 120 by 130 feet (37 by 40&#160;m). The centre of the building contained a 650 feet (200&#160;m) square lightwell with ground glass roof.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESheahan1864572–3_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESheahan1864572–3-22">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPevsnerNeave1995524_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPevsnerNeave1995524-18">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFawcett200186_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFawcett200186-14">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Architect for both buildings was <a href="/wiki/G.T._Andrews" class="mw-redirect" title="G.T. Andrews">G.T. Andrews</a>, and represent his last major commission. The station and hotel were described by some contemporaries as "Hudson's Folly", who thought the scale of the development too great;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGillettMacMahon1980275_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGillettMacMahon1980275-23">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> the station was the largest built in England to that time associated with a railway station.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFawcett200186_14-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFawcett200186-14">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> By the time of completion of the station hotel <a href="/wiki/George_Hudson" title="George Hudson">George Hudson</a>, chairman of the York and North Midland was in disgrace after his fraudulent dealings had been discovered.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFawcett200186_14-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFawcett200186-14">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The Hotel's official opening ceremony took place on 6 November 1851.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESheahan1864572_16-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESheahan1864572-16">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Additional facilities at the station also included a locomotive house, on the west end of north side of the main shed;<sup id="cite_ref-es1_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-es1-24">&#91;map 8&#93;</a></sup> a coal depot to the north-west;<sup id="cite_ref-cd_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cd-25">&#91;map 9&#93;</a></sup> and a turntable.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> A new engine shed was constructed in the 1860s, and a 20 engine shed was constructed in the mid 1870s.<sup id="cite_ref-hshed_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hshed-27">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;n 4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1853 <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a> visited the town, and the use of the station hotel given to the corporation for the accommodation of the royal party; a <a href="/wiki/Throne_room" title="Throne room">throne room</a> was created on the first floor, and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Households_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Royal Households of the United Kingdom">royal household</a> accommodated on the second. The royal party including the Queen, <a href="/wiki/Albert,_Prince_Consort" title="Albert, Prince Consort">Albert, Prince Consort</a> and five royal children arrived on the <a href="/wiki/British_Royal_Train" title="British Royal Train">Royal Train</a> on 13 October 1853 at Paragon Station. The visit concluded with a dinner at the Hotel on 14 October.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESheahan1864180–191_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESheahan1864180–191-31">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="NER_period_.281854.E2.80.931923.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="NER_period_(1854–1923)">NER period (1854–1923)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hull_Paragon_Interchange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: NER period (1854–1923)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hull_train_station_form_platform_2_(geograph_2596166).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Hull_train_station_form_platform_2_%28geograph_2596166%29.jpg/220px-Hull_train_station_form_platform_2_%28geograph_2596166%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Hull_train_station_form_platform_2_%28geograph_2596166%29.jpg/330px-Hull_train_station_form_platform_2_%28geograph_2596166%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Hull_train_station_form_platform_2_%28geograph_2596166%29.jpg/440px-Hull_train_station_form_platform_2_%28geograph_2596166%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hull_train_station_form_platform_2_(geograph_2596166).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 1904 trainshed (2011)</div></div></div>
<p>In 1853 the <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Dock_Branch_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Victoria Dock Branch Line">Victoria Dock Branch Line</a> had opened in Hull, connecting the <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Dock,_Hull" class="mw-redirect" title="Victoria Dock, Hull">Victoria Dock</a> and a number of stations in Hull on a circular route around the outskirts of the town; the line connected to the existing network at junctions 0.5 miles (0.8&#160;km) west of the station.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETomlinson1915519–20_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETomlinson1915519–20-32">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> This line was doubled in mid 1864 and brought more trains into Paragon: from the <a href="/wiki/Hull_and_Hornsea_Railway" title="Hull and Hornsea Railway">Hull and Hornsea Railway</a> (opened 1864); and from the <a href="/wiki/Hull_and_Holderness_Railway" title="Hull and Holderness Railway">Hull and Holderness Railway</a> (opened 1854<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETomlinson1915522–3,_525_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETomlinson1915522–3,_525-34">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>) via a connecting chord to the Victoria Dock Branch Line.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETomlinson1915606,_612_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETomlinson1915606,_612-35">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Further developments in the 1860s created additional or shorted routes into Paragon; the <a href="/wiki/York_to_Beverley_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="York to Beverley Line">York to Beverley Line</a> was completed in 1865 with the opening of the Market Weighton to Beverley section;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETomlinson1915472,_499,_606,_620_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETomlinson1915472,_499,_606,_620-36">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Hull_and_Doncaster_Branch" title="Hull and Doncaster Branch">Hull and Doncaster Branch</a> to south Yorkshire in 1869;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETomlinson1915608–9,_634_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETomlinson1915608–9,_634-37">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> and the line to Leeds extension was completed, extending the line from Hull to Leeds to the city centre, and allowing through running westward.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETomlinson1915472,_499,_606,_620_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETomlinson1915472,_499,_606,_620-36">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Paragon_Station,_Anlaby_Road,_Kingston_upon_Hull_(geograph_3544478).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Paragon_Station%2C_Anlaby_Road%2C_Kingston_upon_Hull_%28geograph_3544478%29.jpg/220px-Paragon_Station%2C_Anlaby_Road%2C_Kingston_upon_Hull_%28geograph_3544478%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Paragon_Station%2C_Anlaby_Road%2C_Kingston_upon_Hull_%28geograph_3544478%29.jpg/330px-Paragon_Station%2C_Anlaby_Road%2C_Kingston_upon_Hull_%28geograph_3544478%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Paragon_Station%2C_Anlaby_Road%2C_Kingston_upon_Hull_%28geograph_3544478%29.jpg/440px-Paragon_Station%2C_Anlaby_Road%2C_Kingston_upon_Hull_%28geograph_3544478%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3218" data-file-height="2386" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Paragon_Station,_Anlaby_Road,_Kingston_upon_Hull_(geograph_3544478).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Entrance hall and booking office, with inlaid "NER" mosaic floor monogram (2013)</div></div></div>
<p>In 1873 the <a href="/wiki/Manchester,_Sheffield_and_Lincolnshire_Railway" title="Manchester, Sheffield and Lincolnshire Railway">Manchester, Sheffield and Lincolnshire Railway</a> obtained running powers into Hull, and passenger trains from that company running to Paragon from August.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETomlinson1915663–4_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETomlinson1915663–4-38">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> In 1898/9 the <a href="/wiki/Hull_and_Barnsley_Railway" title="Hull and Barnsley Railway">Hull and Barnsley Railway</a> and the NER began work towards constructing a joint dock in Hull (see <a href="/wiki/Alexandra_Dock,_Hull" class="mw-redirect" title="Alexandra Dock, Hull">Alexandra Dock</a>); as part of this cooperation between the two companies the H&amp;BR gave the NER running powers over its line in Hull, and the NER allowed the H&amp;BR to run into and use Paragon station.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETomlinson1915718–721_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETomlinson1915718–721-39">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The growth of traffic was accommodated in the mid 1870s by adding a third middle platform to the trainshed; the outer platforms were also lengthened beyond the shed, and short bay platforms added on either side. The cross platform was widened at the expense of the length of the main platforms; the booking office and parcels offices swapped positions, and the middle portico walled up to create greater enclosed space.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFawcett200188_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFawcett200188-40">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFawcett200545_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFawcett200545-41">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> In 1884/5 the hotel was also expanded, adding room at first floor level by extending westward across a concourse entrance.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFawcett200188_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFawcett200188-40">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> In 1887 a station canopy was added over the ends of the departure (southside) platform that extended beyond the shed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFawcett200545_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFawcett200545-41">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;n 5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In addition to the standard facilities the increased <a href="/wiki/History_of_immigration_to_the_United_States" title="History of immigration to the United States">emigration to the United States</a> in the 19th&#160;century led to the construction of an emigrant station,<sup id="cite_ref-ewr_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ewr-44">&#91;map 11&#93;</a></sup> south-west of the main station, in part due to concerns over public health dangers, such as cholera; the station also enabled more efficient handling of the large numbers of emigrants. The station rooms were built in 1871 to the designs of <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Prosser_(architect)" title="Thomas Prosser (architect)">Thomas Prosser</a>, and extended 1881. Because of its historical significance the building is now grade II listed.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>An extensive enlargement of the station was authorised by the NER board in 1897, as part of the extension programme the station's engine shed facilities were transferred to a new site at <a href="/w/index.php?title=Botanic_Gardens_depot&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Botanic Gardens depot (page does not exist)">Botanic Gardens</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoode199236_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoode199236-49">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-hshed_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hshed-27">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;n 6&#93;</a></sup> the transfer was complete by 1901, and in 1902 work began on the rebuilding of the station; the expansion of the site was northwards towards Colliers Street, and required purchases and demolition of houses south of the street.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFawcett200188_40-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFawcett200188-40">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFawcett200545_41-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFawcett200545-41">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hull_Paragon_,_The_Engineer_11_Feb_1908.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Hull_Paragon_%2C_The_Engineer_11_Feb_1908.jpg/220px-Hull_Paragon_%2C_The_Engineer_11_Feb_1908.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="169" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Hull_Paragon_%2C_The_Engineer_11_Feb_1908.jpg/330px-Hull_Paragon_%2C_The_Engineer_11_Feb_1908.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Hull_Paragon_%2C_The_Engineer_11_Feb_1908.jpg/440px-Hull_Paragon_%2C_The_Engineer_11_Feb_1908.jpg 2x" data-file-width="935" data-file-height="720" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hull_Paragon_,_The_Engineer_11_Feb_1908.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hull Paragon <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;1908</span></div></div></div>
<p>The main station was enlarged to a design by NER architect <a href="/wiki/William_Bell_(architect)" title="William Bell (architect)">William Bell</a>. The extension included a new five span steel platform roof, with a two span roof over the concourse, built by the <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Bridge_%26_Engineering_Company" title="Cleveland Bridge &amp; Engineering Company">Cleveland Bridge &amp; Engineering Co.</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-ps_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ps-19">&#91;map 6&#93;</a></sup> with the offices resited to the east end of the station, facing the station concourse, together with the adjacent Hotel. Half of the new office spaces was taken up by a tiled booking office, with wooden booking windows, and architectural detailing in <a href="/wiki/Faience" title="Faience">faience</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-th_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-th-53">&#91;map 12&#93;</a></sup> The booking office's main entrance faced Paragon Square (Ferensway) accessed under a large iron made <i>porte-cochère</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPevsnerNeave1995524_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPevsnerNeave1995524-18">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFawcett200545–50_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFawcett200545–50-54">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ic_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ic-56">&#91;map 13&#93;</a></sup> The enlarged station opened 12 December 1904.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETomlinson1915761_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETomlinson1915761-57">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> An additional range of buildings was built <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;1908</span> to the south-east of the station, to provide stock rooms for the Hotel.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFawcett2005Fig.3.7,_p.46_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFawcett2005Fig.3.7,_p.46-58">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_Engineer11_February_1908p.160,_col.3_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_Engineer11_February_1908p.160,_col.3-59">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bac_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bac-60">&#91;map 14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;n 7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As built the station had nine platforms under the four southernmost spans of the roof; the northernmost span had facilities for special goods, such as cars and horses, and was screened off from the other four;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFawcett200548_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFawcett200548-62">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> it was served by platform 1, known as the <i>fish dock</i> or <i>fish platform</i>, which was also used for fish.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_Engineer11_February_1908p.161,_cols.1,_3_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_Engineer11_February_1908p.161,_cols.1,_3-63">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> The southern bay platforms, and 1887 platform roof was retained for a total of fourteen passenger platforms; platforms 1–9 also received low level roofs outside the main shed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFawcett2005Figs.3.6_&amp;_3.7,_p.46_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFawcett2005Figs.3.6_&amp;_3.7,_p.46-64">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The original station offices were retained and used as waiting rooms and parcel offices.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFawcett200547_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFawcett200547-65">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1904 the station signalling system was converted to an electro-pneumatic power signalling system – the station had two signal boxes: <i>Paragon Station box</i> was a 143 lever box and was located at the end of platforms 1 and 2;<sup id="cite_ref-plsb_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-plsb-66">&#91;map 15&#93;</a></sup> <i>Park Street box</i>, with 179 levers was located 714 feet (218&#160;m) west of the station.<sup id="cite_ref-ps2_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ps2-67">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pssb_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pssb-68">&#91;map 16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 5 March 1916 during a <a href="/wiki/First_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="First World War">First World War</a> <a href="/wiki/Zeppelin" title="Zeppelin">Zeppelin</a> raid that killed 17, a bomb blast blew out the glass in the station roof.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGillettMacMahon1980376_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGillettMacMahon1980376-69">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="LNER_period_.281923.E2.80.931948.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="LNER_period_(1923–1948)">LNER period (1923–1948)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hull_Paragon_Interchange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: LNER period (1923–1948)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From 1924 passenger trains running from the <a href="/wiki/Hull_and_Barnsley_Railway" title="Hull and Barnsley Railway">Hull and Barnsley Line</a> became able to run into Paragon station with the construction of a connecting chord between the NER and H&amp;BR networks in north-west Hull.<sup id="cite_ref-hbrj_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hbrj-70">&#91;map 17&#93;</a></sup> The H&amp;BR's <a href="/wiki/Hull_Cannon_Street_railway_station" title="Hull Cannon Street railway station">Cannon Street station</a> closed in the same year.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 14 February 1927 it was the site of a head-on train collision (see <a href="/wiki/Hull_Paragon_rail_accident" title="Hull Paragon rail accident">Hull Paragon rail accident</a>) in which 12 passengers were killed and 24 seriously injured, caused by a signalling error.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1931–32 the hotel was internally revamped, and expanded by the addition of an extra storey of rooms on the roof, replacing staff bedrooms; and by cement rendered wing on either side of the main entrance; an <a href="/wiki/Art_deco" class="mw-redirect" title="Art deco">art deco</a> entrance onto the station concourse was also added.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFawcett200186_14-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFawcett200186-14">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFawcett2005198–199_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFawcett2005198–199-74">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
A railway museum was established by Hull Museums director <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Sheppard_(curator)" title="Thomas Sheppard (curator)">Thomas Sheppard</a> in the station in 1933.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-museum_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-museum-76">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hull_Paragon_Signal_Box_-_geograph.org.uk_-_255631.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Hull_Paragon_Signal_Box_-_geograph.org.uk_-_255631.jpg/220px-Hull_Paragon_Signal_Box_-_geograph.org.uk_-_255631.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="185" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Hull_Paragon_Signal_Box_-_geograph.org.uk_-_255631.jpg/330px-Hull_Paragon_Signal_Box_-_geograph.org.uk_-_255631.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Hull_Paragon_Signal_Box_-_geograph.org.uk_-_255631.jpg/440px-Hull_Paragon_Signal_Box_-_geograph.org.uk_-_255631.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="539" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hull_Paragon_Signal_Box_-_geograph.org.uk_-_255631.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1930s signal box (2006)</div></div></div>
<p>In 1935 the decision was made to resignal the station and approaches, replacing the 1904 electro-pneutmatic power signalling system with an electrically operated system. "Park Street" and "Paragon station" signal boxes were to be replaced with a single box; the running lines out of the station, including those controlled by the <i>West Parade signal box</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-wpsb_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wpsb-77">&#91;map 18&#93;</a></sup> were to be <a href="/wiki/Track_circuit" title="Track circuit">track circuited</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ps2_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ps2-67">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;n 8&#93;</a></sup> The system was an early British example of electrical interlocking. 48 points were controlled, using thumb switches in the signal box.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Power supply was from the <a href="/wiki/Hull_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Hull Corporation">Hull Corporation</a> at 400&#160;V 50&#160;Hz three phase, with a backup generator powered by a 28 horsepower (21&#160;kW) <a href="/wiki/Petters_Limited" title="Petters Limited">Petter oil-engine</a>. The main external system was electrified at 110&#160;V AC, with shunt signals at 100 or 55&#160;V AC; the point motors, previously electro-pneumatically operated were retained, with a 50 cubic feet (1.4&#160;m<sup>3</sup>) per hour 80 pounds per square inch (550&#160;kPa) max. pressure compressor system, duplicated for redundancy.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Signalling was electric lamp backlit.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Westinghouse_Brake_and_Signal_Company_Ltd" title="Westinghouse Brake and Signal Company Ltd">Westinghouse Brake and Signal Company Ltd</a> was the main supplier of the equipment.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> A new signal box was installed,<sup id="cite_ref-psb_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-psb-83">&#91;map 19&#93;</a></sup> a LNER type 13, resembling in architectural design the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Railway_(UK)" title="Southern Railway (UK)">Southern Railway</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Streamline_Moderne" title="Streamline Moderne">Streamline Moderne</a></i> signal boxes, but with square corners.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/Hull_Blitz" title="Hull Blitz">Hull Blitz</a> of 1941 the station received direct hits on the night of 7 May, with many incendiary bombs hitting the roof. The signal box was badly damaged when a <a href="/wiki/Parachute_mine" title="Parachute mine">parachute mine</a> exploded nearby<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> during the same night the station's small railway museum was destroyed by fire.<sup id="cite_ref-museum_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-museum-76">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="BR_period_.281948.E2.80.931995.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="BR_period_(1948–1995)">BR period (1948–1995)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hull_Paragon_Interchange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: BR period (1948–1995)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Paragon_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_603999.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Paragon_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_603999.jpg/220px-Paragon_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_603999.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Paragon_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_603999.jpg/330px-Paragon_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_603999.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Paragon_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_603999.jpg/440px-Paragon_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_603999.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Paragon_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_603999.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Station entrance with <i>Paragon House</i> above (2003)</div></div></div>
<p>The main entrance canopy was replaced by an office building <i>Paragon House</i> in 1962.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPevsnerNeave1995524_18-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPevsnerNeave1995524-18">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFawcett2005212_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFawcett2005212-86">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ic_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ic-56">&#91;map 13&#93;</a></sup> The building was originally used as a regional headquarters for <a href="/wiki/British_Rail" title="British Rail">British Rail</a>, but was unused in later years.<sup id="cite_ref-ht_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ht-87">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1965 the <a href="/wiki/Newington_branch_line" class="mw-redirect" title="Newington branch line">Newington branch</a> which had been used by trains running from west of Hull to Bridlington and beyond was closed and replaced by a new chord near Victoria crossing.<sup id="cite_ref-wpnj_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wpnj-88">&#91;map 20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-arj_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arj-89">&#91;map 21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoole198649_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoole198649-90">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> The roofs sheltering platforms 1–9 outside the main shed were removed in the 1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFawcett200550_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFawcett200550-91">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 1980s a new "travel centre" (booking and information office) was added on the station concourse. The body of the building was faced with light sandstone, with lighting via semicircular arched windows, and an approximately <a href="/wiki/Barrel_roof" title="Barrel roof">barrel roofed</a> skylight. In the same period a <a href="/wiki/Clerestory" title="Clerestory">clerestory</a> roofed waiting room was added at the head of the station platforms, an architectural homage to both Victorian trainshed roofs and <a href="/wiki/Clerestory_carriage" class="mw-redirect" title="Clerestory carriage">clerestory carriages</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFawcett2005p.236;_Plate_15.10,_p.237;_Colour_Plate_77,_p.239_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFawcett2005p.236;_Plate_15.10,_p.237;_Colour_Plate_77,_p.239-92">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After the privatisation of <a href="/wiki/British_Transport_Hotels" title="British Transport Hotels">British Transport Hotels</a> in the 1980s the "Royal Station Hotel" was renamed <i>Royal Hotel</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-ht_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ht-87">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Post_privatisation_period_.281995.E2.80.93present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Post_privatisation_period_(1995–present)">Post privatisation period (1995–present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hull_Paragon_Interchange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Post privatisation period (1995–present)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1990 the hotel was gutted by a fire,<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> the interior was rebuilt and the hotel re-opened in 1992.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPevsnerNeave1995524_18-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPevsnerNeave1995524-18">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Paragon_Station_under_renovation_-_geograph.org.uk_-_289258.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Paragon_Station_under_renovation_-_geograph.org.uk_-_289258.jpg/220px-Paragon_Station_under_renovation_-_geograph.org.uk_-_289258.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Paragon_Station_under_renovation_-_geograph.org.uk_-_289258.jpg/330px-Paragon_Station_under_renovation_-_geograph.org.uk_-_289258.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Paragon_Station_under_renovation_-_geograph.org.uk_-_289258.jpg/440px-Paragon_Station_under_renovation_-_geograph.org.uk_-_289258.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="430" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Paragon_Station_under_renovation_-_geograph.org.uk_-_289258.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Station front during redevelopment, after demolition of 'Paragon House' (2006)</div></div></div>
<p>In 2000 outline planning permission was given for a transport interchange and shopping and leisure complex near Ferensway, Hull; in 2001 full planning documents were submitted for works on a 42-acre (16.8&#160;ha) site included a new shopping arcade development incorporating a hotel and car parking facilities; a transport interchange incorporating the station; as well as landscaping, setting out of streets, a petrol station and a housing development.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELondon_&amp;_Amsterdam_(Ferensway)_Ltd2001Overview_Statement,_§1-1.5,_pp.1–2_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELondon_&amp;_Amsterdam_(Ferensway)_Ltd2001Overview_Statement,_§1-1.5,_pp.1–2-95">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> The development also included new facilities for the <a href="/wiki/Hull_Truck_Theatre" title="Hull Truck Theatre">Hull Truck Theatre</a> and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Albermarle_Music_Centre&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Albermarle Music Centre (page does not exist)">Albermarle Music Centre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELondon_&amp;_Amsterdam_(Ferensway)_Ltd2001Overview_Statement,_§3.5,_p.4_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELondon_&amp;_Amsterdam_(Ferensway)_Ltd2001Overview_Statement,_§3.5,_p.4-96">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> The shopping development is known as <a href="/wiki/St_Stephen%27s_Hull" title="St Stephen&#39;s Hull">St Stephen's shopping centre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pg_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pg-97">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> The interchange fully opened on 16 September 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-open2007_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-open2007-98">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Features of the railway 2007 station redevelopment include a new canopy to the Ferensway entrance;<sup id="cite_ref-pg_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pg-97">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ic_56-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ic-56">&#91;map 13&#93;</a></sup> the "Paragon House" office block was demolished as part of the redevelopment.<sup id="cite_ref-ht_87-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ht-87">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> The former station booking office area was restored, and in 2009 opened as a community area.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> From 2009 a <a href="/wiki/Mobility_scooter" title="Mobility scooter">mobility scooter</a> hire service was provided at the station.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> The interior of the booking office is used (2011) as a branch of <a href="/wiki/WH_Smith" class="mw-redirect" title="WH Smith">WH Smith</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ht_87-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ht-87">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The new transport interchange was officially opened by the <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Prince_Philip,_Duke_of_Edinburgh" title="Prince Philip, Duke of Edinburgh">Duke of Edinburgh</a> when they unveiled a plaque on 5 March 2009 after arriving at the station on the <a href="/wiki/British_Royal_Train" title="British Royal Train">Royal Train</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A £65,000 bronze statue of Hull resident poet <a href="/wiki/Philip_Larkin" title="Philip Larkin">Philip Larkin</a> by <a href="/wiki/Martin_Jennings" title="Martin Jennings">Martin Jennings</a> was unveiled on the concourse of Hull Paragon Interchange on 2 December 2010, marking the 25th anniversary of the poet's death. The statue was located near to the entrance to the Station Hotel, a favoured watering place of the poet.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, an additional five slate roundels containing inscriptions of Larkin's poems were installed in the floor around the statue;<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> and in 2012 a <a href="/wiki/Memorial_bench" title="Memorial bench">memorial bench</a> was installed around a pillar near the statue.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2017 a full-size model of the Gipsy Moth aircraft used by <a href="/wiki/Amy_Johnson" title="Amy Johnson">Amy Johnson</a> to fly solo from Britain to Australia, created over a six-month period by inmates of <a href="/wiki/Hull_Prison" class="mw-redirect" title="Hull Prison">Hull Prison</a>, was put on display at the station.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> This remained throughout the <a href="/wiki/Hull_UK_City_of_Culture_2017" title="Hull UK City of Culture 2017">City of Culture</a> but moved to the adjacent <a href="/wiki/St_Stephen%27s_Hull" title="St Stephen&#39;s Hull">St Stephen's shopping centre</a> in March 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> The station underwent a revamp during 2017, with a £1.4&#160;million investment providing a new waiting area and more retail units.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Station_Masters">Station Masters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hull_Paragon_Interchange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Station Masters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable plainlinks">This list is <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Lists#Incomplete_lists" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Lists">incomplete</a>; you can help by <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hull_Paragon_Interchange&amp;action=edit">expanding it</a>.</div>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 18em; -webkit-column-width: 18em; column-width: 18em;">
<ul><li>William Woodcock <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;1850</span></li>
<li>George Akrigg <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;1866</span> – 1882<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup></li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Bus_and_coach_station">Bus and coach station</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hull_Paragon_Interchange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Bus and coach station">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="History_and_description">History and description</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hull_Paragon_Interchange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: History and description">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox vcard" style="width:22em;width: 25.5em;"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold"><div style="display: table; width: 100%; border-collapse: collapse"><div style="display: table-cell; width: inherit; vertical-align: middle"><div style="display:inline" class="fn org">Hull Paragon Interchange</div></div><div style="display:table-cell;vertical-align:middle;padding-left:3px;white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Bus_transport_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Bus transport in the United Kingdom"><img alt="BSicon decoding="async" width="300" height="257" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Bus_station%2C_Hull_Paragon_Interchange.jpg/450px-Bus_station%2C_Hull_Paragon_Interchange.jpg Hull">Hull</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Bus stands</th><td>38 bus stands + 4 coach stands</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Bus operators</th><td><a href="/wiki/East_Yorkshire_Motor_Services" <div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hull_Bus_Station_2004_prior_to_being_demolished_(geograph_3048274).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Hull_Bus_Station_2004_prior_to_being_demolished_%28geograph_3048274%29.jpg/220px-Hull_Bus_Station_2004_prior_to_being_demolished_%28geograph_3048274%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Hull_Bus_Station_2004_prior_to_being_demolished_%28geograph_3048274%29.jpg/330px-Hull_Bus_Station_2004_prior_to_being_demolished_%28geograph_3048274%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Hull_Bus_Station_2004_prior_to_being_demolished_%28geograph_3048274%29.jpg/440px-Hull_Bus_Station_2004_prior_to_being_demolished_%28geograph_3048274%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1067" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hull_Bus_Station_2004_prior_to_being_demolished_(geograph_3048274).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1930s Collier Street bus station (2004)</div></div></div>
<p>A bus station was built adjacent to Paragon station in 1935, at a cost of £55,000 on land freed by <a href="/wiki/Slum_clearance" title="Slum clearance">slum clearance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A new bus station integrated with the main railway station was developed and constructed in the first decade of the 21st&#160;century. (see also §<a href="#Post_privatisation_period_(1995–)">Paragon station post privatisation</a>.)
</p><p>Hull Paragon Interchange opened on Sunday 16 September 2007 combining rail and bus station services on a single site. The bus terminal has 38 bus and 4 coach stands, replacing a separate 'island' bus station;<sup id="cite_ref-open2007_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-open2007-98">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> the site of the former Hull Bus Station, adjacent to the north of the railway station now forms part of the <a href="/wiki/St_Stephen%27s_Hull" title="St Stephen&#39;s Hull">St Stephen's shopping centre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> The bus ranks are located at the north of the station, in a "saw-tooth" arrangement. The entrance to the station is from Ferensway, and a reversing roundabout was provided at the west end of the station.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELondon_&amp;_Amsterdam_(Ferensway)_Ltd200101_00913_PO-DRAWINGS-347163,_Sheet_3,_&quot;Proposed_Site_Plan&quot;_(Job_2836,_Drawing_SK-010,_Revision_A)_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELondon_&amp;_Amsterdam_(Ferensway)_Ltd200101_00913_PO-DRAWINGS-347163,_Sheet_3,_&quot;Proposed_Site_Plan&quot;_(Job_2836,_Drawing_SK-010,_Revision_A)-119">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ltp_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ltp-120">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> The station has approximately 1,700 bus departures per day (September 2010).<sup id="cite_ref-ltp_120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ltp-120">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> The area under the northernmost span of the trainshed roof was converted into the concourse and queueing area for the bus station.<sup id="cite_ref-ht_87-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ht-87">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pibc_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pibc-121">&#91;map 22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Services">Services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hull_Paragon_Interchange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bus_services">Bus services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hull_Paragon_Interchange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Bus services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Bus services run from the station to all areas of Hull, as well as to the <a href="/wiki/East_Riding_of_Yorkshire" title="East Riding of Yorkshire">East Riding</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_Lincolnshire" title="North Lincolnshire">North Lincolnshire</a>. Most city bus services are operated by <a href="/wiki/Stagecoach_East_Midlands" title="Stagecoach East Midlands">Stagecoach East Midlands</a>, whilst <a href="/wiki/East_Yorkshire_Motor_Services" class="mw-redirect" title="East Yorkshire Motor Services">East Yorkshire Motor Services</a> is the main bus company for services to the East Riding. Services to <a href="/wiki/North_East_Lincolnshire" title="North East Lincolnshire">North East Lincolnshire</a> are operated by <a href="/wiki/Stagecoach_East_Midlands" title="Stagecoach East Midlands">Stagecoach East Midlands</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Stagecoach_Grimsby_East_Midlands&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Stagecoach Grimsby East Midlands (page does not exist)">Stagecoach Grimsby East Midlands</a>.
</p><p>More distant service include <a href="/wiki/Beverley" title="Beverley">Beverley</a>, <a href="/wiki/York" title="York">York</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scarborough,_North_Yorkshire" title="Scarborough, North Yorkshire">Scarborough</a>, <a href="/wiki/Withernsea" title="Withernsea">Withernsea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Humberside_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Humberside International Airport">Humberside International Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scunthorpe" title="Scunthorpe">Scunthorpe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grimsby" title="Grimsby">Grimsby</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leeds_City_bus_station" title="Leeds City bus station">Leeds City bus station</a>. Other, smaller operators include Alpha Bus,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and Coach and <a href="/wiki/HCT_Group" title="HCT Group">HCT Group</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail_services">Rail services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hull_Paragon_Interchange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Rail services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Hull Paragon is managed by <a href="/wiki/TransPennine_Express" title="TransPennine Express">TransPennine Express</a>, serving mainly its <a href="/wiki/North_TransPennine" class="mw-redirect" title="North TransPennine">North TransPennine</a> route as well as multiple <a href="/wiki/Northern_(train_operating_company)" title="Northern (train operating company)">Northern</a> routes. Additional services are provided by <a href="/wiki/Hull_Trains" title="Hull Trains">Hull Trains</a> and <a href="/wiki/London_North_Eastern_Railway" title="London North Eastern Railway">London North Eastern Railway</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/TransPennine_Express" title="TransPennine Express">TransPennine Express</a> operates a Monday-Saturday service of one train per hour to and from <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Piccadilly_station" title="Manchester Piccadilly station">Manchester Piccadilly</a> via <a href="/wiki/Leeds_railway_station" title="Leeds railway station">Leeds</a>, and one early morning train to <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Airport railway station">Manchester Airport</a> per day. Direct services to and from Manchester are less frequent after 7pm. In May 2017, a later direct service to Manchester Piccadilly will be introduced. On Sunday, a similar service runs at a reduced frequency (approximately every one to two hours), starting later and finishing earlier, with no direct service to Manchester Airport.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-New_Services_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-New_Services-125">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Northern_(train_operating_company)" title="Northern (train operating company)">Northern</a>'s weekday service consists of two trains per hour from Hull to <a href="/wiki/Bridlington_railway_station" title="Bridlington railway station">Bridlington</a>, made up of one semi-fast service and one stopping service, with one service per hour continuing through to <a href="/wiki/Scarborough_railway_station" title="Scarborough railway station">Scarborough</a>. Northern also operate one stopping and one fast service per hour to <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield railway station">Sheffield</a>, and hourly to <a href="/wiki/York_railway_station" title="York railway station">York</a>. At peak times there are additional services between Hull and <a href="/wiki/Beverley_railway_station" title="Beverley railway station">Beverley</a>, that stop at <a href="/wiki/Cottingham_railway_station" title="Cottingham railway station">Cottingham</a>. Weekend running is similar, but with reduced frequencies on some routes and all services finishing earlier. Most fast services from Sheffield call at Hull before continuing to Bridlington, although some timetables show these services as separate rather than continuous.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Hull_Trains" title="Hull Trains">Hull Trains</a> operate a weekday service of seven trains in each direction to <a href="/wiki/London_King%27s_Cross_railway_station" title="London King&#39;s Cross railway station">London King's Cross</a>. At weekends this service is reduced, with 6 trains on Saturday, and 5 on Sunday. However, Sunday services will be increased to 6 trains in each direction from December 2017. Every day one train to London starts at <a href="/wiki/Beverley_railway_station" title="Beverley railway station">Beverley</a> progressing onto Hull in the early morning, with one late night train from London terminating at Beverley after Hull.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-New_Services_125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-New_Services-125">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/London_North_Eastern_Railway" title="London North Eastern Railway">London North Eastern Railway</a> operate one train per day Monday-Saturday to <a href="/wiki/London_King%27s_Cross_railway_station" title="London King&#39;s Cross railway station">London King's Cross</a> in the early morning, with the return arriving mid evening. There is only a service arriving from London at mid evening on Sunday.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Platforms">Platforms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hull_Paragon_Interchange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Platforms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hull_Paragon_Interchange&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br /><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Hull+Paragon+Interchange%22">"Hull Paragon Interchange"</a>&#160;–&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Hull+Paragon+Interchange%22+-wikipedia">news</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Hull+Paragon+Interchange%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers">newspapers</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Hull+Paragon+Interchange%22+-wikipedia">books</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Hull+Paragon+Interchange%22">scholar</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Hull+Paragon+Interchange%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">October 2016</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<ul><li><i>Platform 1</i> – A <a href="/wiki/Bay_platform" title="Bay platform">bay platform</a> which is very rarely used.</li>
<li><i>Platform 2</i> – The most used platform with Hull Trains using the platform for services to London Kings Cross. Also used by <a href="/wiki/Northern_(train_operating_company)" title="Northern (train operating company)">Northern</a> services on routes to <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield railway station">Sheffield</a> from <a href="/wiki/Bridlington_railway_station" title="Bridlington railway station">Bridlington</a> or <a href="/wiki/Scarborough_railway_station" title="Scarborough railway station">Scarborough</a> or services from <a href="/wiki/York_railway_station" title="York railway station">York</a> terminating here.</li>
<li><i>Platform 3</i> – <a href="/wiki/TransPennine_Express" title="TransPennine Express">TransPennine Express</a> services terminating from <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Piccadilly_station" title="Manchester Piccadilly station">Manchester Piccadilly</a> along with Platform 4.</li>
<li><i>Platform 4</i> – TransPennine Express services from Manchester Piccadilly.</li>
<li><i>Platform 5</i> – Northern services terminating from Doncaster and also occasionally used for services from York when platform 2 is in use.</li>
<li><i>Platform 6</i> – Northern services from <a href="/wiki/Beverley_railway_station" title="Beverley railway station">Beverley</a> or services terminating here from Sheffield.</li>
<li><i>Platform 7</i> – Northern services from/to Bridlington/Scarborough terminating or from Doncaster/Sheffield. Also used by <a href="/wiki/London_North_Eastern_Railway" title="London North Eastern Railway">London North Eastern Railway</a> to <a href="/wiki/London_King%27s_Cross_railway_station" title="London King&#39;s Cross railway station">London Kings Cross</a> operated by a <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_800" title="British Rail Class 800">Class 800</a> Azuma on Weekdays, and Saturdays, and by a <a href="/wiki/InterCity_125" title="InterCity 125">High Speed Train</a> on Sundays.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Naming">Naming</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hull_Paragon_Interchange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Naming">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Paragon_station,_Hull.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Paragon_station%2C_Hull.jpg/220px-Paragon_station%2C_Hull.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Paragon_station%2C_Hull.jpg/330px-Paragon_station%2C_Hull.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Paragon_station%2C_Hull.jpg/440px-Paragon_station%2C_Hull.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2042" data-file-height="1305" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Paragon_station,_Hull.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Early architect's impression of the proposed station and hotel design (south façade)</div></div></div>
<p>The rail station is commonly known as "Paragon station", "Hull Paragon", or just "Hull station". <a href="/wiki/National_Rail" title="National Rail">National Rail</a> refers to the station as "Hull" (HUL).
</p><p>The name comes from the nearby "Paragon Street" which was itself built <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;1802</span>;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFawcett201085_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFawcett201085-129">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> the name dates back earlier – The Paragon Hotel public house, (now the "Hull Cheese") gave its name to the street, and dates back as far as 1700.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The station was opened as "Hull Paragon Street" 8 May 1848 by the <a href="/wiki/York_and_North_Midland_Railway" title="York and North Midland Railway">York and North Midland Railway</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEButt1995125_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEButt1995125-131">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/North_Eastern_Railway_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="North Eastern Railway (UK)">NER</a> used the name "Hull Paragon",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEButt1995125_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEButt1995125-131">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> however the 'Paragon' suffix was inconsistently used over ninety years from opening to 1948.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since the <a href="/wiki/British_Railways" class="mw-redirect" title="British Railways">British Railways</a> period (1948) the officially used name has usually been "Hull", excluded the 'Paragon' suffix.<sup id="cite_ref-tuf_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tuf-133">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;n 9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The term "Hull (Paragon)" has also been used by <a href="/wiki/Network_Rail" title="Network Rail">Network Rail</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Since redevelopment in 2007 the official name has been "Paragon Interchange"; however as of 2012 timetables continued to use "Hull", except when referring to bus services.<sup id="cite_ref-tuf_133-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tuf-133">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The hotel has been known as the "Station Hotel" or "Royal Station Hotel" from its early history;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESheahan1864201,_563,_577,_605_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESheahan1864201,_563,_577,_605-136">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> after privatisation in the 1980s the owners renamed it "Royal Hotel".<sup id="cite_ref-ht_87-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ht-87">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> As of 2014, as part of the <a href="/wiki/Mercure_Hotels" class="mw-redirect" title="Mercure Hotels">Mercure Hotels</a> group the hotel's official name is the <i>Mercure Hull Royal Hotel</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hull_Paragon_Interchange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: In popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The station has been used as a filming location in the film <i><a href="/wiki/Clockwise_(film)" title="Clockwise (film)">Clockwise</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> in an episode of <i><a href="/wiki/Agatha_Christie%27s_Poirot" title="Agatha Christie&#39;s Poirot">Agatha Christie's Poirot</a></i> "The Plymouth Express"<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> and in the comedy <a href="/wiki/To_Hull_and_Back" title="To Hull and Back"><i>Only Fools and Horses</i> – To Hull and Back</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hull_Paragon_Interchange&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-5">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"An Act for enabling the <i>York and North Midland</i> Railway Company to make a Station at <i>Hull</i>, and certain Branch Railways connected with their Railways and the said Station; and for other Purposes.", (Cap 218, 22 July 1847)<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-15"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-15">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFFawcett2001">Fawcett (2001</a>, p.&#160;84) states 1 April 1847, whilst <a href="#CITEREFHitches2012">Hitches (2012)</a> gives 1 March 1847</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-20"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-20">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFSheahan1864">Sheahan (1864</a>, p.&#160;572) gives ground dimensions of 153 by 125 feet (47 by 38&#160;m) long by wide for the station, which appears erroneous based on the 1856 Ordnance Survey 1:1056 town plans.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-30"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-30">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">A square shed of approximately 150 feet (46&#160;m) square had been constructed north-west of the original shed, south of St Stephen's church and square by the late 1800s.<sup id="cite_ref-ostown_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ostown-28">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-es2_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-es2-29">&#91;map 10&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-43"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-43">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Note. The 1891 Ordnance Survey 1:500 OS Town plan shows the locations of the supporting columns.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-51"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-51">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The station's coal depot was resited to the site of the shed near St Stephens Square.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-es2_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-es2-29">&#91;map 10&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-61"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-61">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The diagram in <a href="#CITEREFFawcett2005">Fawcett (2005</a>, Fig.3.7, p.46) notes a bakery and stock rooms, whilst <a href="#CITEREFThe_Engineer11_February_1908">The Engineer &amp; 11 February 1908</a>, p.160, col.3) notes a motor garage and stock rooms. To the west and south of the 1848 front another building was built at around the same time (OS. 1:2500 1893, 1910/1)</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-78"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-78">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"West Parade" a street between the Park Street and Argyle Street bridges; <i>West Parade Junction</i> was just east of Argyle street bridge, a double diamond crossover (1928), and the point were the Beverley, Hornsea, Withernsea and Selby lines diverged. "West Parade signal box" was just west of the junction and bridge (OS. 1:2500. 1928)</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-134"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-134">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Since the closure of <a href="/wiki/Hull_Cannon_Street_railway_station" title="Hull Cannon Street railway station">Cannon Street</a> to passengers in 1924 the station was the only consistently timetabled rail terminus in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-tuf_133-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tuf-133">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
